Joint Conference of Chambers of Commerce from Various Provinces and Cities Decides to Form a Anti-Smuggling Committee; Representatives Urge Song Ziliang to Abolish Guangdong's Oppressive Taxes; Wang Xiaolai and Others Host a Banquet for Representatives from Various Places Last Night 82

After the opening of the joint conference of chambers of commerce from various provinces and cities the day before yesterday, the meeting continued yesterday morning at 9:00 a.m. A decision was made to organize the Anti-Smuggling Committee of the Republic of China in various places, and Wang Xiaolai and two others were appointed to visit Song Ziliang, the special commissioner of the Guangdong Provincial Finance Department and Director of Finance, to request the abolition of oppressive taxes. The details are recorded as follows:

Representatives Attending Yesterday The representatives attending the meeting yesterday were Yu Xiaochuan, Yuan Yousheng, Cheng Qianyuan, Wang Jingting, Zhou Zishi, Liang Rendao, Wan Zhucun, Cheng Ganqing, Luo Huizong, Yao Zilun, Yuan Duanfu, Zhu Yaoting, Wang Xiaolai, Zheng Longwen, Xu Jilun, Tao Yutang, Wang Yungu, Wang Xiren, Gu Huaibing, Cai Chang, Liang Bingjian, Jia Shaowu, Jin Rongqiao, Gao Bochang, Gu Jingshen, Luo Yuming, Lin Yushen, Gu Suming, Chen Xinyan, Ge Jichen, Liang Jingxuan, Liu Yangshan, Xu Guosen, Ke Ganchen, Jin Runxiang, Du Yuesheng, Luo Qinghua, Liu Wenting, Wang Deting, Xu Xiaochu, and others, totaling 43 people.

Chairman's Report After performing the formalities, the presidium Wang Xiaolai, Yu Rongqiao, and others reported on the review situation of each group yesterday, and the representatives from Changsha, Minhou, and other places who continued to arrive were welcomed. They also reported on the telegram from the Hankou Chamber of Commerce, requesting a discussion on submitting a telegram to the government to postpone the income tax.

Discussion of Proposals After the meeting began in the morning, the discussion of the proposals from the commercial group began. Xu Jilun, the deputy director of the proposal review committee of the commercial group, reported that the group received a total of two proposals, one was the joint liability for partnership debts, and the other was the abolition of disguised likin. The review result was that they should be established and requested the General Assembly to discuss them. After the report, after detailed discussion by the representatives present, it was resolved: (1) Request the Legislative Yuan to amend Article 681 of the Civil Code and adopt the joint liability for partnership debts. (2) Telegraph the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance to effectively abolish disguised likin in various provinces. Next, the telegram from the Hankou Chamber of Commerce was discussed, requesting the government to postpone the income tax. After discussion, it was resolved to telegraph the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance, and Wang Xiaolai, Gao Bochang, Gu Suming, Luo Qinghua, and Yuan Qianyuan were appointed as drafting committee members to draft the telegram, explaining the difficulties in implementing the income tax. Then, the meeting adjourned. At 2:00 p.m., the meeting continued to discuss the proposals from the commodity group. Jin Runxiang, the commodity group proposal review committee member, reported that the group received a total of twelve proposals, which were analyzed into three parts: one was the part on guaranteeing the proper transportation and sale of commodities, the second was the issue of unifying the organization of the national anti-smuggling agencies, and the third was the issue of strict anti-smuggling methods. The review result was that the General Assembly should be requested to resolve and handle them separately. After discussion, it was resolved: (1) Telegraph the government to issue an order to guarantee the normal transportation and sale of commodities. (2) Organize the Anti-Smuggling Committee of the Republic of China in various places to concentrate forces and unify methods. The organizational outline should be drafted by the presidium of the General Assembly together with the representatives of the Jiangxi, Hankou, and Changsha Chambers of Commerce, and the Shanghai representative Luo Qinghua, and then discussed at the next General Assembly. (3) The strict anti-smuggling methods should be submitted to the Anti-Smuggling General Assembly to be made into concrete methods or formulated into regulations based on the proposals of the representatives from various places, and then telegraphed for implementation. As for the postal package part, the meeting telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to forward it to the Ministry of Transportation, ordering the Post Office General Administration to order all post offices to strictly investigate and seize them in accordance with the customs anti-smuggling methods. After the discussion, the draft telegram on the income tax case to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance was passed, and the meeting adjourned.

Visiting Song Ziliang Yesterday afternoon at 3:30, the designated representatives Wang Xiaolai, Yu Rongqiao, Cai Chang, and others, based on the resolutions of the Joint Conference, went to the China Construction Bank to visit Song Ziliang, the newly appointed special commissioner of the Guangdong Provincial Finance Department and Director of Finance. They were received, and Wang Xiaolai first stated the resolutions of the Joint Conference, requesting the abolition of all oppressive taxes. Song indicated that he would adopt them, and the representatives left at about 4:00.

Drafting Committee After the meeting adjourned yesterday, the drafting committee of the Anti-Smuggling Committee of the Republic of China in various places held a meeting. The presidium Wang Xiaolai, Yu Rongqiao, the representatives of the Jiangxi, Hankou, and Changsha Chambers of Commerce, and the Shanghai representative Luo Qinghua attended. They drafted the organizational outline of the Anti-Smuggling Committee and formulated a draft plan, which was dispersed at about 7:00.

Banquet for Representatives Wang Xiaolai and other representatives of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce hosted a banquet for representatives from various provinces and cities at the International Hotel on Jing'an Temple Road yesterday at 8:00 p.m. Wang Xiaolai delivered a speech, and the banquet ended in joy at 10:00. In addition, the National Accountants Association and the Shanghai Accountants Association have scheduled a banquet for representatives from various provinces and cities at the Hua'an Building on Jing'an Temple Road at 12:00 a.m. today.

Song Ziliang and Zou Lin Fly to Guangdong This Morning 83

Organizing Guangdong's Finances and Banking

The Central News Agency reports that the Ministry of Finance has specially appointed Song Ziliang as the Guangdong Finance Special Commissioner in order to thoroughly organize the finances and banking of Guangdong Province. He is scheduled to fly there this morning (the 22nd), and Finance Vice Minister Zou Lin will accompany him. Tang Shoumin, Bei Songsun, and Li Tisheng, the Deputy Director of the Treasury Bureau of the Bank of China, will also go separately. According to the details obtained by the reporter from various parties,

Song Convenes Discussions

After the Ministry of Finance appointed Song Ziliang as the Guangdong Finance Special Commissioner, Song went to the China Construction Bank at about 9:00 a.m. yesterday to handle important matters. Then, he convened Finance Vice Minister Zou Lin, Ye Zhuotang, the Director of the Central Bank, Xi Demao, the Director of the Business Bureau, Tang Shoumin, the General Manager of the Bank of Communications, Bei Songsun, the Manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Bank of China, and others to discuss the organization of the finances and banking of Guangdong Province. The establishment of a branch of the Central Bank was also discussed. They dispersed at about 10:00.

Flying to Guangdong This Morning

According to Song Ziliang, speaking to a Central News Agency reporter, he is scheduled to hire a special plane from China National Aviation Corporation to fly to Guangdong on the morning of the 22nd. After arriving in Guangdong, he will investigate the current financial situation of Guangdong Province in detail. Once he has a clue, he will return north to report, and then go to Guangdong again at a scheduled time. Those who will accompany Song include Bei Songsun, the manager of the Shanghai Branch of the Bank of China, Zhao Jiyan, the assistant manager of the China National Products Bank, and Zhuang Yongling, Song's secretary. Wu Jiantao, the newly appointed Director of the Guangdong-Guangxi-Fujian Regional Unified Tax Bureau, flew from Xun to Beijing yesterday morning, visited Finance Minister Kong to ask for instructions, and took the night train to Shanghai to catch the same plane.

Zou Lin Issues a Statement

A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency specially visited him at his residence on Gaoen Road last night and was received. He answered various questions from the reporter, saying that his task this time in going south was to inspect the general financial situation of Guangdong Province, because at the beginning of a thorough reform, it is necessary to first understand the actual situation. All the detailed methods of the reform plan have not yet been determined. Although the method of reforming the currency system had been largely decided before, it is now different because the political situation in Guangdong Province has changed. As for the reorganization of tax revenue, the central government has long had unified orders, which are the same in all provinces. Furthermore, although the establishment of a Guangzhou branch of the Central Bank and a Guangzhou branch of the Issuance Reserve Committee can be done with a single order, it is necessary to understand the actual situation there before a plan for implementation can be determined. In the future, when it is implemented, the new Director of Finance Song will be responsible. It is impossible to predict how long I will stay here. I will return north at any time after the work is completed. When the reporter asked if he also had to go to Guangxi, Zou said that it would depend on the political situation at that time.

Tang Sets Off This Morning

Regarding the issue of reorganizing Guangdong's currency system, the Ministry of Finance had previously sent Tang Hai'an, the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, to Guangdong twice to make contact. Tang Shoumin and Bei Songsun were said to be going soon, but because Chen Jitang did not cooperate, it was never completed. Now that the political situation in Guangdong Province has stabilized, it has been decided to proceed immediately. Tang is still staying in Hong Kong, while Tang Shoumin is scheduled to take the North German Company's Boston liner this morning. The Bank of China sent Li Tisheng, the Deputy Director of the Treasury Bureau, and Zhou Shouliang, the Deputy Director of the Business Bureau, to accompany him. According to Zhou, speaking to a reporter yesterday, he has decided to take the same plane as Song Ziliang, while Li will travel on the same ship as Tang, along with three Bank of China staff members. The ship is berthed in the Huangpu River and will set sail at about 8:00.

Bank of China Establishes a Branch in Guangdong

According to a person in charge of the Central Bank, Song Ziliang has been appointed to go to Guangdong to investigate and organize the general financial and banking affairs of Guangdong Province. He will act in accordance with the will of the Central Government and handle matters in a practical manner in order to relieve the suffering of the people of Guangdong. Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Notifies All Industries to Organize Private Inspection Branches 86

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce yesterday issued a notice to all industry associations under its jurisdiction to organize private inspection branches for each industry, taking a unified approach. The two notices are recorded as follows: (1) Respectfully announcing that, in order to assist the government in investigating and suppressing smuggling, the Chamber has already organized a Private Inspection Committee that has begun its work. According to Article 11 of the committee's organizational charter, which states, "After the establishment of this committee, the municipal chamber of commerce shall notify relevant industry associations to formulate separate regulations and organize branches, which shall be submitted to this Chamber for public deliberation and implementation," all organizational rules and inspection rules for private inspection branches in various industries have been approved by the second committee meeting. All trade associations related to smuggling should immediately follow the aforementioned resolution, formulate separate regulations based on their respective industry situations, organize private inspection branches, and actively proceed. We are accordingly sending along copies of the organizational rules and inspection rules for private inspection branches in various industries for your reference and action. It is essential that your esteemed association examine and handle this matter, and submit draft branch organizational charters, formulated in accordance with the regulations, to this Chamber for record and implementation within ten days of receiving this letter. (2) Respectfully announcing that, regarding the matter of assisting the government in investigating and suppressing smuggling, the methods of implementation for various industries in this city have already been determined by the Private Inspection Committee established by this Chamber, which has also notified various industries to organize private inspection branches to be led and managed by the committee. As member associations of this Chamber, trade associations in various industries should maintain a unified approach and avoid discrepancies in handling private inspection matters. Fearing that various industries have not paid attention to this matter, it has been resolved at the second Private Inspection Committee meeting to notify all industry associations that matters related to private inspection should be handled in accordance with the resolutions of this Chamber, so as to ensure uniformity. We are accordingly issuing this notice and request your esteemed association to take note and act accordingly.

A Beggar from the Northeast Donates Money to Purchase an Airplane 87

Accumulated One Yuan Through Three Months of Saving

The Shanghai Municipal Fundraising Committee of the China Aviation Association's Expanded Aviation Patriotic Movement to Purchase Airplanes as a Gift to the Government for Chairman Chiang's Fiftieth Birthday received a letter yesterday from a beggar in Hexi Xinxiang, Northeast, who signed his name. He stated that he was disabled in the war of resistance, his left arm was broken, and he could not serve, so he begged for a living. Now that he learned of the purchase of airplanes to present to the government to celebrate Chairman Chiang's birthday, he expressed his deep sympathy. However, feeling that his heart was willing but his strength was insufficient, he specially donated one yuan, accumulated through three months of begging and saving, along with nine jiao, one fen, and eight li in national currency, with the remainder used for postage and remittance fees. Please accept it. The beggar's wartime injury and begging for a living, not forgetting his patriotism, and raising funds for three months to donate for the purchase of airplanes to celebrate the birthday, is truly commendable. Compared to the general wealthy and unbenevolent, who do not contribute a single penny, only know their own comfort, and have no enthusiasm for saving the country, there is a world of difference. It is said that the association has already accepted the donation and thanked him.

Also, the Airplane Commemoration Society continued to receive donations of one hundred yuan from Mr. Zhang Rangzhi, thirty-one yuan from Zhu Yulu and Xu Yongsheng, twenty yuan from the gentry, merchants, and people of Rushankou, Shandong, seventy-two yuan, one jiao, and five fen from Lin Liangeng, He Huan, and Mao Jiu'an of the Dalai Company's Harrison ship, thirty yuan each from the Yimiao stallholders association and the Qixing Copper Smelting Plant, and twenty yuan from the Qixing Copper Plant's workers' union. The enthusiastic support from all walks of life is evident.

Hai Zhen and Gong Ping to Resume Sailing to Shantou and Guangzhou Today 88

Both Cargo and Passengers are Full

The Zhaoshangju's Sihai steamer stopped operations on the 11th of this month and announced it would sail to Shantou and Guangzhou, and stopped selling passenger tickets to Shantou and Guangdong from Shanghai. After more than ten days, because the Guangdong affairs have been peacefully resolved, Zhaoshangju has received instructions from the Ministry of Communications to have the Sihai steamer resume its Shantou-Guangdong route as soon as possible to avoid losses from the suspension. The bureau immediately decided to have the Haizhen steamer be the first to resume the Shantou-Guangdong route, starting today. Passengers, upon hearing the news, rushed to buy Shantou-Guangdong passenger tickets, and they were sold out in a short time. As for the goods of the Guangdong and Shantou merchants that had been suspended due to exchange rates, there was too much accumulated in Shanghai. Now that the Guangdong exchange rate has risen again and the overall situation has been settled, a large batch of goods was rushed to be loaded to Shantou and Guangdong. After the Haizhen was fully loaded, the Gongping steamer was also specially used to transport export goods to Shantou and Guangzhou, and it was also fully loaded. Both ships are going to Guangdong today. This is the first national ship to go to Guangdong after the suspension of Shanghai national ships.

Gold Exchange Opened Yesterday Morning. Brokers Held a General Meeting 93

The Shanghai Gold Exchange's issue of increasing handling fees was settled after Chairman Xu Busheng of the board of directors and Chairman Zhan Liansheng of the Brokers' Association reached an agreement. It was stipulated that a handling fee of one jiao would be levied on each lot, and a bonus of two fen and five li would be given to the brokers. However, the transaction on that day would be levied at half price, and it would be trialed for three months. The Brokers' Association issued a notice yesterday morning, advising all brokers to operate as usual. The brokers accepted the advice and started operating as usual from 9 am. The opening price for September futures was 1,132.4 yuan, and the closing price was 1,132.3 yuan. The Brokers' Association held a temporary general meeting of all members at the association on North Wuxi Road at 2 pm yesterday. More than 60 brokers attended. Chairman Shan Liansheng reported on the agreement reached with Chairman Xu Busheng of the board of directors on the remedy for handling fees. The discussion began immediately. The case of handling fees of one jiao per lot and a bonus of two fen and five li to brokers, but the transaction on the day will be levied at half (person per share) and the broker's bonus will also be calculated as half (one fen and two faces per person) was resolved and approved. A broker made a transaction on the standard gold customer case of each trade, and each broker expressed his opinion. After a long period of discussion, there was no result due to divergent opinions. Finally, the speaker Zhang asked the brokers to handle it themselves. It was not dismissed until about 5 pm.

Czech Astronomer Hujer Arrives in Shanghai from Japan to Talk About the Philosophical View of Astronomy 96

According to the Continental News, Czech astronomer Dr. Hujer recently went to Hokkaido, Japan, with Czech and other foreign scientists to observe the solar eclipse. Now he is passing through Shanghai on his way home. Although the doctor has not been famous for long, he has already given lectures in the United Kingdom, the United States, Mexico, India, Soviet Russia, and other countries in Europe. His specialty is the philosophical view of astronomy. In the past four or five years, he has lectured on this issue no less than 400 times in various places. The doctor told customers that astronomers cannot support themselves by traveling, but it is enough to combine the work and speech. So he can travel to all parts of the world to observe our noisy world. Today's world is in a terrible turmoil, especially in the so-called civilized countries. Science today has the task of fulfilling its obligations, especially astronomy. In the past, scientific knowledge has focused on destructive work. Scientists in the new era must now realize this and use their great power to engage in construction work. Science, as a thing, has only been used casually so far, just like children playing with new toys. However, I have learned the secret of the long-term existence of ancient civilization on this trip to the East, and the so-called civilization of Qin and West is now gradually reaching a precarious point. There are various misnomers in Qin and West's civilization. They certainly know how to invent objects to enjoy many pleasures and conveniences, but this so-called civilization actually contains barbarism everywhere. For example, Japan has certainly mastered the essence of industry and machinery. Japanese people love skyscrapers and complex industrial structures very much and imitate them very hard. Try to do bizarre skills, but Japanese people have not yet captured the essence of Western civilization. India lives under philosophy, and this philosophy is almost incomprehensible to Westerners. Mahatma Gandhi's passive resistance is completely inconsistent with the grand tone of Western culture, so many people cannot understand it. Gandhi and other leaders of Jiadu's failure to rashly adopt Qin-Western civilization is enough to be considered. What is literature? Many people do not yet know that the Earth is a very small part of a large universe. Science can make us realize that people in the entire game and structure of the universe are actually relatively unimportant. The legend that the doctor lived in India for a year and had close ties with Juxiong Gandhi, philosopher Tagore, and other Indian leaders. Before going to India, he studied Sanskrit. After arriving in India, he widely used this knowledge. His book about India will be published soon. During the 1932 solar eclipse, Professor Mitchell of the University of Virginia invited the doctor and American experts to Quebec, Canada, to observe together. Four years later, he lived in the United States and often engaged in research at the Yerkes Observatory of the University of Chicago. He was also invited by the Mexican government to study the astronomy of the ancient civilization of Zhongxiwan. Before going to the United States, he gave a lecture for a year at the Imperial College of Science in England. Now he plans to stay in Shanghai for a few days, then go to Beijing to inspect the Observatory of the new capital, and then go to the old capital to inspect the Observatory in the southeast corner of the ancient city. After completing his official duties, he will return to his country via Manchuria and Soviet Russia.

Japanese Merchants Buy Wheat from Exchange, Sell for Profit; No Recent Purchases of Rice Reported 99

Regarding the issue of Japanese merchants buying and selling grain, a reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency yesterday morning revisited Mr. Huanxin, who stated that Japanese merchants purchasing rapeseed from China and transporting it to Japan for oil extraction is a common occurrence every year. The Japanese Mitsuyoshi Trading Company purchases wheat from Wuhu and transports it to Qingdao and other places to supply flour mills, because Chinese wheat is cheaper than foreign wheat, involving about 20,000 to 30,000 yuan. The Japanese Toyoi Trading Company purchased wheat from the Shanghai Exchange and has already made a profit, selling it back on the exchange. As for buying rice, there have been no recent reports of such activity.

Number of Overseas Chinese Expelled in Half a Year Totals 199; Mostly from Japan and Canada 100

Due to the global economic downturn and the exclusion of overseas Chinese in various countries in recent years, many overseas Chinese have experienced business failures, and the number of unemployed is particularly high. As a result, many have been forced to pack their bags and return home. In the first six months of this year, a total of 199 expelled overseas Chinese landed in Shanghai, including 119 men and 17 women. The largest number returned from Japan, totaling 117. The next largest group returned from Canada, totaling 33. This was followed by 14 returnees from Vancouver, British Columbia, 9 from Victoria, British Columbia, and 1 each from Mexico, the Soviet Union, and Taiwan. It is also reported that a larger number of overseas Chinese are landing in Xiamen.

Ministry of Communications Orders Telegraph Bureau to Maintain Long-Distance Telephone Lines; Instructs on Line Repair Methods to Avoid Impeding Long-Distance Calls 101

The Ministry of Communications issued an order to the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau stating that when telegraph lines experience blockage, the temporary use of thin wires for connection should be replaced immediately with the original type of wire.

Repair and reinforce the lines properly. The Ministry had previously issued order No. 4692 on September 27, 1935, and instruction No. 4718 on September 30 of the same year, promulgating the "Methods for Repairing Obstructions on Telegraph Lines," which clearly stipulated the relevant regulations.

The Ministry's long-distance telephone lines are gradually increasing, and the security of military communications is extremely important, requiring diligent maintenance. If the line balance is slightly off, problems such as induced noise will occur, making clear communication difficult. Therefore, special attention should be paid to the above-mentioned repair methods, and no negligence is allowed. Also, the

crossing positions and methods of each telephone line have been properly configured and should not be changed in any way. Detailed diagrams should be provided to instruct the workers in charge of each section to be familiar with the number of pairs and the crossing positions and methods of the telephone lines under their jurisdiction to avoid errors. When line workers test the lines, they must do so on the

test line poles equipped with test line clamps, and after the test, the test line clamp must be thoroughly cleaned and tightened. Do not arbitrarily cut the lines. Furthermore, the Ministry has long-standing regulations regarding the locations where long-distance telephone lines enter the bureau. Other intermediate bureaus must not arbitrarily cut the lines or connect other single lines to avoid hindering long-distance calls. All are expected to comply and instruct others to comply.

Guangdong-Guangxi Inspection Group Releases Findings 102

The Xinxin News Agency reports that the inspection report of the Guangdong-Guangxi Industrial Inspection Group, organized by the business community of this city this spring, has been compiled and was officially released yesterday. Excerpts of the key points are as follows:

Guangdong's Industry

In Guangdong, large-scale factories are all within the scope of provincial operation. Industrial construction in Guangdong is the most important part of the three-year plan. The factories established in Guangdong over the past two years aim to meet the needs of society while also considering the original artisans, so that their livelihoods are not taken away by the rise of mechanical industry. The industries established in Guangdong in the past two years have all adhered to this principle. The Xicun First Industrial Zone includes chemical industries such as sulfuric acid, sodium bicarbonate, ammonia, phosphate fertilizer, potash fertilizer, cement, beer, and soda factories. Henan is the Second Industrial Zone, including textile industries such as cotton spinning, woolen weaving, silk spinning, and ramie silk spinning factories. Guangdong is a unique sugar-producing region in the country. To achieve national self-sufficiency in refined sugar, the entire province has been divided into five sugarcane cultivation zones, dedicated to revitalizing the sugar industry, starting with Guangdong, Huizhou, Chaozhou, and Shantou, and then expanding from there. Each sugar factory will also establish a distillery to replace gasoline, a paper mill to manufacture newsprint and various stationery, a beverage factory to produce beer and soda, and a wood gas generator factory to save fuel for vehicles. A hemp bag factory will also be established to supply packaging for cement, rice, and other grains. Other projects, such as the steel factory, the Wengjiang Hydroelectric Plant, and the Huangpu Shipyard, are all in the planning stages. All of the above factories are able to meet the needs of the province and were established for the people who lack the resources to create them themselves. The total cost is over 40 million yuan. Taking the cement factory as an example, between 1930 and 1931, the average daily import of cement was 50 barrels, with a selling price of 13.5 yuan per barrel, resulting in an annual loss of 24.3 million yuan. Since the establishment of the Xicun Cement Factory, it initially produced 1,200 barrels per day, and now, with expanded machinery, it can produce over 3,000 barrels per day, priced at 10 yuan per barrel. As a result, the price of imported cement has also decreased. It is estimated that the Xicun Cement Factory can recover 30,000 yuan in lost profits per day, or 10.8 million yuan per year. The users enjoy the 6.3 million yuan in profits from the price reduction. Therefore, the Xicun Cement Factory alone can prevent the outflow of over 17 million yuan annually. Additionally, the annual import of foreign sugar into Guangdong is approximately 30 million yuan. It is currently estimated that the sugarcane cultivation zones in Guangzhou, Chaozhou, and Huiyang can collectively produce over 6,000 dan of sugar per day, or over 2 million dan of sugar per year, which is more than enough to meet the needs of the entire province. This will recover 30 million yuan in outflowing funds annually. Furthermore, in recent years, Guangdong's mulberry and silk industries have declined, leaving people with no means of making a living. If the sugar industry is revived, there will be a greater need for sugarcane, and farmers can convert their mulberry fields to sugarcane cultivation. If they lack capital, the provincially operated sugarcane cultivation zones can provide loans. Based on an annual output of 2 million dan of sugar, with 10 dan of sugar requiring one mu of sugarcane, a total of 200,000 mu of sugarcane will be needed. With each household cultivating ten mu of sugarcane, this can support 20,000 households. With five people per household, this can support 100,000 people. If all five cultivation zones are fully established in the future, in addition to meeting Guangdong's own needs, they can also be sold throughout the country, and the annual recovery of outflowing funds will be over 30 million yuan. Moreover, the number of farmers who can rely on this for a living will be even greater. Furthermore, after the establishment of the various factories, they will accommodate many workers. It is estimated that the Xicun Cement Factory and its affiliated Henan Kiln Factory, as well as the three sugarcane cultivation zones, can accommodate approximately 5,000 workers. If we include other workers involved in quarrying and transportation, with an average of five people per household, this can support 40,000 people. This does not include other factories.

Guangxi's Agriculture

Guangxi is located in the southwest of China, on the frontier, with obstructed transportation. Agriculture accounts for 70% to 80% of the economy, and industry remains in the handicraft era. Work is simple and only for use in the province. In recent years, the import of industrial goods from home and abroad has increased sharply. The methods are sophisticated, and the prices are low, which has made the province's only nascent handicraft industry unable to compete, and it is gradually being eliminated. In order to seek self-reliance and save the backward industry, the Guangxi authorities have established sulfuric acid plants, tung oil plants, alcohol plants, tannery, printing plants, and machinery plants, which have modern tool scale. Guangxi has a vast land, humid climate, and is suitable for planting. It is indeed an agricultural province. Food crops include rice, wheat, corn, etc. Rice can be harvested two to three times a year in Guinan. Corn can also be planted twice. Root crops include sweet potatoes and water chestnuts. Legumes include black beans, soybeans, broad beans, etc. Fibers include jute, ramie, and cotton. Other special crops include peanuts, rapeseed, sugar cane, indigo, and tobacco. In terms of fruits, there are pomelos, chestnuts, oranges, tangerines, lychees, longans, cantaloupes, pineapples, etc. In terms of forest products, pine, fir, tea, tung, cassia are suitable for planting in northern Guangxi, and camphor, star anise, cinnamon, Phoebe zhennan, etc. are suitable for planting in the south. There are industrial raw materials and medicinal plants with economic value. Camphor can be extracted from camphor trees, which are the most widely used products in modern chemical industry and are also excellent raw materials for manufacturing explosives. Its relationship to national defense is also very important. Guangxi's natural environment for agriculture is so superior, and agricultural and forestry products are so abundant. However, due to the backwardness of farmers' production technology and the limitations of social capital, it has not been fully developed. For example, rice can be harvested twice a year in central Guangxi, but due to the lack of water conservancy facilities, irrigation in autumn is extremely difficult, so few farmers plant late rice. In the northwest mountainous areas, due to transportation difficulties, surplus grains cannot be exported, and even if they are exported, it is not economical. As a result, farmers' cultivation is extremely crude, and they fail to make full use of the land. At present, the provincial government is making every effort to promote agricultural affairs. It has established an agricultural experiment station in Liuzhou. Wen Anhua will go to the injury to watch. The scale is grand and the results are remarkable. There is also a forest reclamation area that was formerly held by Mr. Wu Tingfang, and there are also achievements. Another agricultural and forestry demonstration area is located at the headquarters of eight militia district cadres schools, and it is expected that the results of the total injury experiment, such as seed selection, cultivation, fertilization, processing, and breeding, will be gradually transmitted from the demonstration injury to the militia cadres students. These students, after leaving school and returning to their hometowns, will serve as village chiefs and principals of national basic schools, and they will transmit it to farmers, which is convenient and easy to popularize. In recent years, livestock, rice, grain, and tung oil have been the main commodities for small exports. If they can be good at promoting charcoal and increase production, the export volume will increase day by day. Guangxi is most lacking in cotton, and combing cloth and cotton yarn are the main imports every year. A cotton cultivation experiment injury has been established to try to restore the inherent cotton production. Iron ore and hardware are quite valuable. Coal is available but not produced. The mines that have been opened, such as tin in Fuchuan, He County, Zhongshan, Hechi, and Nandan, crane in Gongcheng, Fuhe, and Duan, money in Guixian and Hechi, gold in Youjiang, Wuming, Daling, and Jiejiang, are increasing in output every year. Therefore, although Guangxi is known as a poor province, the underground minerals and the agricultural crops on the ground are both sources of wealth. If we can recruit technical talents on the one hand and utilize foreign capital on the other hand to engage in development, then in a few years, why is it difficult to turn a poor and barren area into a rich province?

Guangdong-Guangxi Commerce

The commercial construction in Guangdong includes the Tungsten Ore Monopoly Bureau and the Provincial Products Management Office. Tungsten ore production is concentrated in Guangdong, Hunan, and Jiangxi. The tungsten ore used in various countries in the world is supplied by these three provinces, accounting for nearly 70% or more. Its use in manufacturing tungsten steel is important. The Guangdong provincial government considers tungsten to be important for foreign trade and of great importance to national defense, so it is specifically nationalized and implements a controlled policy to prevent merchants from competing freely, causing prices to fall, and profits to accrue to foreign merchants. Moreover, the selling power is controlled by the government, which can adapt to the times and not affect national defense. Since the implementation of the monopoly, the price of tungsten has increased by four or five times to seven or eight times compared with the past. The government uses the profits to carry out production projects, and merchants also enjoy the benefits of increased convenience. The Guangdong government believes that if the provincial factories were to take on both manufacturing and sales, it would not only be distracting but also lead to many drawbacks. Therefore, it has specifically established the Provincial Products Management Office as a sales organization, dividing it into four departments: spinning, cement, sugar, and fertilizer, each with its own responsibilities. The collection and payment of funds are handled by the bank, with each department cooperating and sharing responsibilities, which can avoid malpractices. In addition, the Management Office can also act on behalf of merchants to sell domestic goods. Although the city's commerce is in a slump, it is still better than Shanghai. The China National Goods Company has a turnover of 3,000 yuan per employee, and the turnover of Wing On, Sincere, and The Sun is also not bad. In the future, with the unification of the currency system and convenient remittances, Guangdong's commerce will have even more hope. Guangxi is a province with an import surplus. Its position in foreign trade is equivalent to that of China in the world market. Its exports are mostly agricultural products and raw materials, and its imports are all industrial products or semi-finished products. Wuzhou is located in the lower reaches of the Xijiang River, reaching Qi and Qian upstream, and connecting Hong Kong and Guangdong downstream. Goods come and go through this place, holding the total trade of the province. Its location is the same as that of Shanghai. All cities in the interior of Guangxi have an import surplus to Wuzhou, while Wuzhou has an import surplus to Hong Kong and Guangdong. On the other hand, due to the slump in the world market and the decline of rural Guangxi in recent years, Guangxi's total trade volume has not only failed to grow naturally, but has also declined to some extent. However, the degree of decline in exports is more severe than that in imports, so the amount of the import surplus has increased significantly. In general, an increase in the import surplus does not necessarily indicate economic decline, but in Guangxi, the import surplus not only indicates the depth of foreign goods, but also because the province has no intangible income to offset it, the result of the import surplus is the outflow of silver and the depletion of finance, which is a major obstacle to Guangxi's economic development.

Zhou Baixing Sentenced to Six Years for Beating Grandfather to Death; Sentence Reduced Because Defendant Was Under 18 103

Zhou Shaoqing, a 65-year-old farmer from Zhoujiazhai, Sanlintang, Pudong, had a grandson named Zhou Baixing, 19, who was a habitual gambler. On the night of June 1 of this year, he returned home after losing money gambling and demanded money from his grandfather, Zhou Shaoqing. When his grandfather rebuked him, Baixing became enraged and beat his grandfather. Unfortunately, the injuries were fatal, and Shaoqing died immediately. Baixing fled to Shanghai, seeking refuge at the home of his father-in-law, Zhou Xuegen, at 139 Luxue Lane, Bailinan Road, West Shanghai. His wife reported him to the police, who arrested him and handed him over to the local court. The prosecutor charged him with causing the death of a senior relative through assault and battery and brought a public prosecution. After the debate concluded, presiding Judge Chen Kangsun sentenced Zhou Baixing at 12 noon yesterday for causing the death of a senior relative through assault and battery. Considering that he was under 18 years old, the sentence was reduced according to the provisions of the criminal law, and he was sentenced to six years of imprisonment as a warning. After the sentencing, he was taken back into custody to await the expiration of the appeal period before being sent to prison.

Representatives of Shanghai East and West Slum Dwellers Petition Various Parties Yesterday 104

Slum dwellers in the East and West districts of Shanghai have been ordered to demolish their homes within a limited time by the Municipal Council in order to improve the city's appearance. Following a joint meeting, Tang Anping, Wang Gongfeng, Liu Huairen, Hu Yumen, Xu Yiqun, and 24 others were selected as representatives. At 2 PM yesterday, they went to the First Special District Citizen's Association at Tianhougong Bridge to request relief. Chen Jiufeng, the executive member of the association, received them. The representatives stated their intentions, saying that in this time of economic downturn, they have no way to make a living and no ability to return to their hometowns. They have been forced to build sheds as temporary shelters, and the hardship of their lives is self-evident. The municipal authorities should quickly seek to revive the economy and provide relief to workers so that the common people can live in peace. However, the Municipal Council has not only failed to show compassion but has taken advantage of people's desperation, forcing slum dwellers to demolish their homes within a limited time to improve the city's appearance. The news has spread, causing panic among the old and young. They requested that the association uphold justice and advocate for the slum dwellers, asking the Municipal Council to withdraw its order and allow them to avoid demolition in order to reassure the people. They are willing to guarantee that they will not build any more additions in the future and requested that the Municipal Council quickly construct civilian housing so that slum dwellers will have a place to live when landlords take back their land or the Municipal Council builds roads. In this way, the Municipal Council can achieve twice the results with half the effort in improving the city's appearance. Mr. Chen then expressed his acceptance of the representatives' opinions and promised to be responsible for negotiating with the Municipal Council. If it can be guaranteed that no further additions will be built, it may not be difficult to resolve the issue. He asked them to wait patiently and not take any actions outside of the proper channels. The representatives left satisfied. They then petitioned the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession, where Secretary Tao Leqin received them and promised to argue their case reasonably and strive to achieve their goals. He also advised the slum dwellers to wait patiently for a resolution. The representatives then went to the Municipal Council to petition, where Director He Dekui received them. He replied that the Municipal Council had tentatively decided to demolish the slum dwellings in various districts, but the overall plan would be decided after further discussion.

Lodger Turns Robber: Ms. Ai Ai Robbed; Losses of Clothing, Diamond Rings, and Cash Exceed 10,000 Yuan; Live-in Lodger Also Tied Up and Robbed 105

Ms. Ai Ai (Fu Wenhao), a famous socialite from Sichuan, was robbed at her home yesterday morning at around 6 AM by four lodgers renting the attic room on the fourth floor, who made off with clothing, diamond rings, and cash worth over 10,000 yuan. Details are recorded below:

Enjoyed Great Fame

Fu Wenhao, a Sichuan woman, is currently 35 years old. Ai Ai is her pseudonym. More than ten years ago, Ms. Ai was a famous socialite in Shanghai, and she once appeared on the silver screen, gaining great fame. Afterwards, she gradually disappeared from the public eye. However, when people in society occasionally mentioned Ms. Ai Ai, they could all recall her vividly.

Renting Out Remaining Rooms

Ms. Fu currently resides in a Western-style house at 72 Avenue Albert, French Concession, occupying the second floor. Because she has few family members, she rented out the attic room on the second floor to Ms. Li Anna (32 years old) and the third floor to Ms. Huang Chen (45 years old) from Fujian. A week ago, Ms. Fu, seeing that the room on the fourth floor was also unused, posted a rental advertisement in order to save money and attract tenants.

Four Lodgers

The day after the rental ad was posted, two young men in Western suits claiming to be students at the Dapuqiao Political Science College went to rent the room. Ms. Fu thought the young men looked like students and immediately agreed, and they moved in that day. However, two more people came along, making a total of four (three in Western suits and one in Chinese attire). Ms. Fu did not suspect anything.

Robbery in the Early Morning

Unexpectedly, at around 6 AM yesterday morning, when Ms. Fu and the other tenants were still asleep, the four young men on the fourth floor suddenly rushed downstairs. Three of them were holding pistols. They tied up Ms. Fu and each of the tenants and robbed them at will. After about 45 minutes, they fled with their loot without a trace.

Reporting to the Police for Investigation

When Ms. Fu and the other tenants realized that the bandits were gone, they shouted for help. Neighbors heard the cries and rushed over to untie them. They immediately reported the incident to the French police station. The police chief sent Chinese and Western detectives to investigate. It was estimated that clothing, diamond rings, and cash worth about 10,000 yuan had been stolen, with Ms. Fu suffering the greatest losses. The French police are currently conducting a thorough investigation.

Typhoon Touches Shanghai 107

550 Nautical Miles from Shanghai; Direction Indicates it Will Pass Outside Daji Mountain

Of the two typhoons that originated in the South Pacific, one has already dissipated, while the other is heading towards the Chinese coast. If its current direction remains unchanged, Shanghai may be affected by the typhoon, and the situation is gradually attracting attention. According to a report from the Datong News Agency, yesterday a reporter inquired with the Xujiahui Observatory and learned that the typhoon originated east of the Philippines (north of Yap Island). At 6 AM yesterday, it had advanced to within a 60-nautical-mile radius of 127 degrees east longitude and 23 degrees north latitude (550 nautical miles from Shanghai, and 360 nautical miles east of Taiwan Island). However, its direction is towards the north-northwest. If this remains unchanged, the typhoon will likely pass outside Daji Mountain near the Wusongkou harbor, and Shanghai may be affected by the edge of the typhoon. The strength of the wind is still unclear.

Industrial Electricity Rates for Zhabei Water and Electricity Company 108

Request for Discount from National Goods Association Denied

The China National Goods Maintenance Association had previously requested a preferential rate for industrial electricity from the Zhabei Water and Electricity Company, citing the high prices, in order to revive the market and save industry. The Association received a reply yesterday indicating that this was difficult to implement. Details are as follows:

Reply to Maintenance Association

Dear Sirs, We have received your letter requesting a 30% discount on electricity and water rates for Zhabei industries in order to maintain commerce, etc. Our company has always paid close attention to assisting commercial and industrial enterprises. The water rates we set are already lower than those in the British and French concessions. Recently, in light of the economic downturn, we have revised our business electricity sales regulations, reduced electricity prices, and adopted a tiered billing system, which is particularly beneficial to industrial electricity users. We have enclosed a copy for your reference. Regarding the merchant's request, it is difficult to comply due to cost limitations. We hope you will understand and inform the association.

New Electricity Rates

In order to benefit businesses, the company has made the following new rules (1) Electric motors that consumers install, up to 50 horsepower, will be billed on a monthly basis depending on the amount of horsepower connected. Lower prices are available for those who use more electricity with the following rates (a) The first 50 kilowatt hours (kWh) is ¥.06 per kWh; the next 100 kWh (51-150 kWh) is ¥.055 per kWh; the next 100 kWh (151-250 kWh) is ¥.04 per kWh; the next 100 kWh (251-350 kWh) is ¥.03 per kWh, and any kWh over 350 is billed at ¥.025 per kWh. For factories with over 50 horsepower usage, a separate contract will be drawn up and prices can be negotiated (2) Deep-well pumps, irrespective of horsepower or amount used, will be billed at ¥.08 per kWh (3) Electric vehicle charging will be calculated according to the tiered rates listed above (4) Use of alternating current cranes and hoists will be billed according to the tiered rates listed above.

Public Concession Death and Birth Statistics for Last Month 109

The Municipal Council's Health Department released statistics. A total of 1,001 births were reported in June, of which 943 occurred within the Public Concession, including 500 male infants and 443 female infants. 55 births were reported for foreigners, of which 57 were born to residents of the Public Concession, including 25 male infants and 32 female infants. There were 44 deaths among foreigners in June, with non-Chinese Asians accounting for 59%. The leading causes of death were pneumonia, tuberculosis, suicide, eczema, and cerebral congestion. The death rate among the Chinese was 14 per thousand. The leading causes of death were old age, tuberculosis, typhoid fever, pneumonia, and bronchitis.

US Army Lieutenant Colonel, Johnson, Commits Suicide. Recent Suicides of Americans in Shanghai, Including This One, Totals Three 110

According to the "Great American Evening Post," Lieutenant Colonel Johnson of the US Army, attached to the Philippine Army, aged 52, resided on the fourth floor of a large hotel. This morning (the 21st), around 2:10 AM, he suddenly jumped from his bedroom window and died upon impact. The incident was immediately reported to the police, who in turn reported it to the US authorities. The body was sent to the International Funeral Parlor for examination on Wednesday afternoon. A letter addressed to his wife in the Philippines was found in his bedroom, stating that he was committing suicide out of necessity and asking for forgiveness. The US authorities in Shanghai have telegraphed his wife and the Army Department in Washington. He had been involved with the Philippine Boy Scouts for several years, serving as their commander, a position usually filled by US government officers or Filipinos in the regular army. He arrived in Shanghai on the "General Pershing" mail ship from Manila on Monday afternoon and checked into the hotel in the evening. The reason for this rash act is unknown. This marks the third suicide by an American resident in Shanghai in recent days.

After the Tong Yi Trust Company ceased operations, the First Special District Court accepted the application from Xu Yeji and others to declare Tong Yi bankrupt, ruling for bankruptcy. The regulations were as follows: (1) Tong Yi Trust Company was to be declared bankrupt on July 17, 25th year [of the Republic of China] at 11:00 AM; (2) Bankruptcy administrators: Accountant Li Ding and Lawyer Li Mian; (3) The period for filing claims was from July 17 to September 30; (4) The date of the first creditors' meeting was August 15 at 9:00 AM; (5) Address: Lake Society, Guizhou Road, Beijing Road. Tong Yi held a shareholders' meeting yesterday, and various creditors petitioned for compensation. Details are as follows:

Shareholders' Meeting

The Tong Yi Trust Company held an extraordinary shareholders' meeting at the Bankers' Association on Hong Kong Road at 2:00 PM yesterday. More than twenty shareholders attended, including Guo Yuyuan and Zhou Shouliang, representing 1,380 shares. Those present included the former liquidator, Accountant Xi Yushu, and Lawyer Li Zuyu. Guo Yuyuan reported that the number of shares present met the legal requirement, and the meeting was declared open. The chairman first reported on the operational difficulties that led to the cessation of business and the court's bankruptcy ruling. Then, discussions began on: (1) Ratification of the previous board of directors' decision to cease operations, which was passed; (2) Ratification of the previous establishment of a liquidation office, which was passed; (3) Ratification of the previous settlement plan, which was passed; (4) Acceptance of the First Special District Court's bankruptcy ruling, which was passed. The meeting adjourned around 4:00 PM.

Creditors' Petition

The Compensation Group organized by creditors of Tong Yi Trust Company gathered more than one hundred creditors at 3:00 PM yesterday. They prepared a petition and went to the extraordinary shareholders' meeting of Tong Yi at the Bankers' Association on Hong Kong Road to petition the shareholders. Representatives were elected, including Tuan Zongxing, Xing Minyi, Liu Donghai, Zhu Zao Rui, Zhang Kelun, Qiu Fengbao, Jiang Menggu, and Sun Cheng, to attend and observe. The purpose of the petition was to demand full payment within the time limit ordered by the Ministry of Finance and to request a clear response. After the meeting, shareholders' representatives Xu Jiliao and Zhou Shouliang met with them and reported on the shareholders' meeting resolutions and the acceptance of the court's bankruptcy ruling, advising them to wait for the court to handle the matter according to law. The petitioners dispersed at 5:00 PM.

The Two Cases Against Liu Huizhi to be Merged for Trial; If Found Criminally Liable, Liu Will Be Deemed a Repeat Offender 112

Liu Huizhi, former general manager of the China Industrial Bank, has been repeatedly criminally prosecuted by shareholders of the bank for embezzlement and breach of trust since his resignation. Recently, five shareholders, including He Jiechun, Weng Pengnian, Yan Xiaoquan, Zhu Ruping, and Yan [], jointly filed a lawsuit against Liu, listing eight instances of Liu's misconduct, involving embezzled funds amounting to as much as four to five million. Two court sessions had been held to summon and question him, as previously reported. Now, because presiding judge Tan Xinzhen found that five of the eight charges brought by He and others were related to the facts alleged in Zhang Chongfu's lawsuit, the criminal part of that case had been temporarily suspended by the presiding judge and transferred to the civil court to resolve the civil issues first. Since He's lawsuit had similarities with Zhang's, for the sake of clarifying the facts, it was deemed necessary to cross-reference them. Therefore, yesterday morning, both plaintiffs and defendants were summoned to inquire about the progress of the civil part of Zhang Chongfu's lawsuit in the civil court. Liu Huizhi's defense lawyer stated that the civil part of the case had already concluded with two trials and was now final. Therefore, the criminal part of the case could proceed, and the civil court's judgments from both trials were submitted for review. Judge Tan then informed both parties that the only matter to be examined today was this, and the case itself would be investigated on a separate date. However, it is said that the court, in order to emphasize procedure and facilitate future trials, intends to merge the lawsuits filed by Zhang Chongfu and He Jiechun for trial. If the defendant is found criminally liable, he will be considered a repeat offender, and separate judgments will not be necessary.

After the Municipal Council's Reply, the Ant Society Sends Another Letter of Negotiation 115

Cultural Groups Performing Non-Commercial Shows; Regulations Do Not Require Licenses

Xin Sheng Society reports that the Public Concession Municipal Council has illegally interfered with the performance of patriotic dramas. The Ant Society's Experimental Small Theater Group sent a letter of protest to the Municipal Council and received a reply stating that it was based on the regulations for music academy licenses. Since the Ant Society did not sell tickets for the performance, the Council's citation of the regulations was inappropriate. Yesterday, they specially requested assistance from Chinese directors Jiang Yiping and Zhang Yichen of the Citizens' Association. The National Drama Association also convened a meeting for this purpose and decided to issue a declaration of support. The Ant Society yesterday also entrusted lawyers Sha Qianli and Yang Tianxun to send a letter of negotiation to the Municipal Council, the original text of which reads: "Dear Sirs, we have received your letter K417 of the 6th of this month, stating that according to Article 8 of the regulations for theater and music academy licenses, all licensees must submit detailed programs to your office before the performance to determine whether the performance complies with the license. The Ant Society, which our clients belong to, is a cultural organization registered with the Shanghai Municipal Government's Education Bureau and filed with the Ministry of Education of the National Government's Executive Yuan and is not a commercial organization. On June 23 of this year, the society gave a dramatic performance as a guest at Lake Society, this was merely an annual event to invite members and their families, in order to strengthen relationships and raise funds, and the performance date was only one day, so it cannot be compared with commercial theaters. Our clients are one of the taxpayers in the Public Concession, and are bound to comply with the relevant regulations within the Concession, namely the Shanghai Public Concession Land Regulations and its appendices, but after searching these regulations, there is no requirement to obtain a license for a non-commercial cultural group like our clients putting on a theatrical performance once a year. Even in terms of Appendix 34, opening a theater requires a license, and since our clients are not opening a theater, there is no obligation to obtain a license. Therefore, Article 8 of the theater and music academy license regulations mentioned in your office's reply cannot be applied to our clients. Furthermore, our clients performed dramas in the Public Concession on June 3, 1934, and June 16, 1935, without obtaining licenses beforehand, and your office not only did not prohibit the performances but also sent personnel to the venue for protection. Your office has completely acknowledged in the past that these public welfare and entertainment performances do not require licenses. This time, you have suddenly prohibited them, illegally imposing restrictions beyond the provisions of the Public Concession Land Regulations, depriving our clients of their freedom to perform, and violating the law. This is beyond belief. Our clients have entrusted us, the lawyers, to lodge a serious protest with your office. As for all the losses suffered by our clients due to your office's illegal prohibition, we reserve the right to demand compensation. At the same time, we hereby notify your office that our clients will exercise the rights of taxpayers on August 2 and continue to perform in the Public Concession, and your office must not prohibit them again illegally. Whether your office can comply with the Land Regulations will be determined by this. We are hereby sending this letter on behalf of our clients, hoping for your attention and a clear reply. Addressed to the Director-General of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council."

French Forensic Institute Sends Personnel to Examine Gu Zhuxuan's Opium Addiction to Determine Whether It Has Been Broken; Report to be Issued 123

Gu Zhuxuan from Yancheng was arrested for instigating murder. Dissatisfied with the Second Special Court's sentence of imprisonment, he appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court. During the trial period, while detained in the external ward of Guangci Hospital due to illness, he bribed the head guard to smoke opium. He was reported by a prisoner and prosecuted by the French Police Affairs Department, sentenced to eight months' imprisonment. Gu, dissatisfied, appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court. Later, the High Court merged the murder case and the opium case for trial. On the 26th of last month, the court ruled that he was innocent in the murder case, but maintained the original eight-month sentence in the opium case. In addition, according to the newly promulgated regulations on prohibiting opium and drugs, he was sentenced to one year's deprivation of civil rights and ordered to quit opium addiction within two months. Subsequently, Gu submitted a petition to the Third Branch of the High Court, claiming that his opium addiction had been broken, with a certificate from a medical officer, requesting exemption from being sent to a rehabilitation center. After the opium case was finalized, he was sent to prison for execution. Gu submitted two more petitions to the Third Branch of the High Court, requesting the court to suspend his personal custody during the appeal period for the murder case and allow him to post bail, and to exempt him from the sentence in the opium case. As previously reported, Acting Presiding Judge Zhu of the High Court held a hearing some days ago, bringing Gu to the court for questioning and informing him of the requested points. Now, it has been learned that Gu, while serving his sentence, had his progress in breaking his opium addiction examined by prison medical officers, who reported it to the Third Branch of the High Court. After receiving the report, the High Court consulted the Zhenru Forensic Institute, requesting them to send personnel to re-examine Gu Zhuxuan's opium addiction to determine whether he had indeed broken it. A forensic officer surnamed Chen from the Forensic Institute came to Shanghai yesterday morning and went to the Second Special District Prison on Avenue Massenet to take Gu Zhuxuan for examination and assessment. The results are expected to be revealed soon.

Autopsy Performed on Two Apprentices Burned to Death 124

Lawyers' Association Building Clubhouse Report 125

The Shanghai Lawyers' Association Building Clubhouse Committee (members: Shen Junru, Jiang Yiping, Chen Tingrui, Sun Zuji, Xu Zuoliang, Yu Chengxiu, Yu Chuiluo, Tan Yigong, Qu Yue, Zha Renwei, Wang Weizhen) submitted a written report to the Executive Supervisory Committee regarding the progress of the committee yesterday. The original report is transcribed below: "Since the committee was commissioned by the Executive Supervisory Committee at the zero-five meeting and established on September 1 of last year, it has actively carried out the work of building the clubhouse, holding a total of thirteen meetings. Initially, it was planned to purchase land separately for construction. Therefore, advertisements were placed to solicit land. Although more than 30 submissions were received, after review, only three locations were considered slightly suitable: (1) Between Weihaiwei Road and Rue Massenet; (2) Behind the Huaan Company on Rue Amiral Bayle; and (3) Rue Luzon. However, due to the high prices during inspections and negotiations, it was difficult to meet the budget. The association had too much debt and could not make a decision. Therefore, it was proposed at the 210th meeting of the Executive Supervisory Committee on October 23 of last year that the construction should still be carried out at the original site. Subsequently, according to this resolution, we began soliciting architectural drawings and hired architectural experts Zhang Xiaoliang, Zhang Jiguang, and Jiang Changgeng as architectural consultants to the committee. They attended the meetings. A total of 27 architectural drawings for the clubhouse were received and publicly displayed at the association for seven days. Subsequently, the selections were made according to the legal methods. Only fourteen were selected in the first review, six were selected in the second review, and the selections were reduced to three in the third review. In the fourth meeting, through voting, the drawing prepared by the Dingzhong Engineering Office was selected at the eleventh meeting of the Building Committee on April 9 of this year. It was approved by the 222nd joint meeting of the Executive Supervisory Committee on April 15 of this year. On April 17, the twelfth meeting of the Building Committee resolved to hand over the architectural project details to the original applicant for the tender, so that the project could be advertised. At present, the applicant, Dingzhong Engineering Office, is working overtime to rush the engineering details. According to reports, most of the more than forty architectural details have been completed and will be delivered in the coming days. This is the past work situation of the committee, and a summary report is submitted as above. Addressed to the Executive Supervisory Committee of the Shanghai Lawyers Association."

Assassination of Gu Bingjun. Four Defendants Sentenced After Appeal. Acquitted During First Trial 126

Gu Bingjun (also known as "Big Hook"), a foreman at the Shanghai West Public Welfare Yarn Factory, was suddenly shot and killed in November 1927 in front of the Kouweiyu Sauce Garden in Cunshan Lane, Caojiadu. The perpetrators remained at large for several years. It was not until September of last year that the accomplices of the perpetrators, Yuan Aliang, revealed the matter after drinking, which was learned by the family members of the deceased, Gu Bingsong and Gu Cui. They reported it to the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, who, together with Public Concession detectives, arrested the perpetrators, Zhao Chunquan (also known as "Little Overlord"), the chief foreman of the Public Welfare Yarn Factory, and his brother Zhao Bingquan (also known as "Maomao"). They were escorted to the First Special Court for interrogation and handed over to the Shanghai Local Court for trial. Subsequently, the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau arrested two more accomplices, Gu Fafa and Lu Xisheng, and handed them over to the Local Court. In the first trial, all four defendants, Zhao Chunquan and others, were acquitted. Prosecutors Tang Ruxiu and Lei Binzhang, expressing their dissatisfaction, appealed to the High Court, listing their reasons. The family of the deceased also hired lawyers Chen Xingmin and others to appear in court. Judge Siwen of the High Court began investigating the case and, after three months of investigation and trial, issued a verdict on the morning of the 20th of this month, overturning the original judgment regarding the acquittal of Zhao Chunquan and others. Zhao Chunquan and Zhao Bingquan were each sentenced to sixteen years' imprisonment, and Gu Fafa and Lu Xisheng were each sentenced to ten years' imprisonment.

Rickshaw Puller Dies After Fight Over Two Cents in Debt. External Examination of the Body Unable to Determine Cause of Death. Judge Orders Autopsy by Forensic Doctor for Further Review 127

Gu Chuncai, a 48-year-old man from Funing residing at No. 10 Yuxing Lane, Gujiawan, Zhabei, earned his living by pulling a rickshaw, but he was not registered with the authorities. Therefore, he was not supposed to pull a rickshaw, but Gu usually waited for others to hand over their shifts and then continued pulling the rickshaw in order to make a living. However, around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, Gu was waiting for rickshaws to hand over their shifts on the side of North Sichuan Road and Qiujiang Road with four companions. At this moment, Gu suddenly asked one of the four companions to return the two cents he was owed. A quarrel ensued, followed by a brawl. Gu, being weak, was unable to resist and fell to the ground. The assailant and the other three people fled the scene. Subsequently, Officer 238 of the Dixwell Road Police Station, passing by, noticed the situation. In addition to sending his rickshaw to Tongren Hospital for treatment, he also reported to the police station, which ordered Chinese Detective Fan Defu and Detective Mu Chunrong to investigate the scene. Gu died at 6:40 PM due to the ineffectiveness of the treatment. The body was taken to the forensic examination institute on Avenue Petain. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Zhang Zongru, assigned by the First Special District Court, accompanied by two forensic doctors, Wei Zhang and Wang Zuyi, and court clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the institute to examine the body. He then took the bench in the public hall. First, the detectives reported the details of the incident. Then, the deceased's wife, Li Shen, and her son, Da Kouzi, reported to the court, claiming that the deceased had gone out around 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon and suddenly died. They requested that justice be served by arresting the perpetrator and bringing him to justice, adding that their family was poor and unable to afford to claim the body. Witness Pan Zhu, a small vendor, testified that she was selling socks near the scene on that day and only saw the deceased wrestling with another person. Later, she did not see it because someone bought something. Because the external examination of the body was unable to determine the cause of death, Zhang ordered the forensic doctor to perform an autopsy on the body and then review the case. Because the family was unable to claim the body, the body was handed over to the Pushan Villa for burial after the examination.

Last Month, Three Deaths from Malaria in the Public Concession - Special Circumstances in Shanghai Make Mosquito Eradication Difficult 129

According to the Public Works Department's health report for June, malaria was the most noteworthy infectious disease in the Concession that month. Worryingly, three people died from malaria. The increase in gastrointestinal diseases, such as typhoid fever and dysentery, was also higher than the previous month. Fortunately, cholera had not yet broken out, and preventive measures were still being diligently implemented. There were also many measles cases, but the number decreased by fifty-eight compared to the previous month. Although summer had just begun, there seemed to be fewer flies this year compared to last year, but mosquitoes were extremely rampant, especially in the eastern and western suburbs. In June, there were eleven foreign malaria cases, with six residing in the eastern district and five in the Zhaofeng Garden and Hongqiao area. There were twenty-one Chinese malaria cases, with sixteen residing in the eastern district and the rest in the western district. All deaths from malaria were Chinese. Mosquito eradication efforts were more difficult in Shanghai due to conditions different from other major cities. For example, the outskirts of Shanghai were full of rice paddies, and the standing water in the fields was a breeding ground for mosquito larvae. The Public Works Department's release of fish fry into rice paddies was an important part of mosquito eradication efforts, but when the rice paddies dried up, the small fish had to be collected. Unfortunately, farmers often let them die. Furthermore, the pits created when digging foundations for buildings in Shanghai also provided breeding grounds for mosquito larvae. There was no immediate solution to these special circumstances. Among the reported cases of typhoid fever, there were ten foreign cases and sixty-four Chinese cases. Over ninety percent of those affected had not been vaccinated, and the three or four who had been vaccinated had received the vaccine more than two years prior. Therefore, typhoid fever vaccinations should not be neglected. Fortunately, citizens were becoming increasingly aware of this, and the health department was overwhelmed with vaccination requests. It was reported that 47,786 people were vaccinated in mid-June.
